They're split\\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \\\"use strict\\\" code. The \\\"use strict\\\" bit is stored in\\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\\n48:  *\\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\\n50:  * different groups of flags:\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"are we parsing strict code?\\\", and so\\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\\n57:  * \\\"returned up\\\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"did we see a use strict\\n58:  * directive\\\"?\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\\n63:  *\\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\\n90:  *\\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\\n93:  *\\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\\n96:  *\\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\\n103:  */\\n104: \\n105: class JSFunction;\\n106: class JSObject;\\n107: class JSScript;\\n108: struct Certain limitations of\\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\\n28:  *\\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\\n30:  *\\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\\n35:  *\\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\\n37:  *\\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\\n49:  *\\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\\n54:  * to \\\"create an arguments object for a function\\\" obviously varies between\\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\\n58:  *\\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\\n61:  * further below).\\n62:  *\\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\\n64:  *\\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\\n67:  *\\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\\n78:  *     character type.\\n79:  *\\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\\n81:  * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n84:  * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\\n85:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive.  As\\n86:  * noted above, this field's existence separate from that in ParserBase\\n87:  * motivates the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameters on various token stream\\n88:  * classes.\\n89:  *\\n90:  * Everything in PerHandlerParser *could* be folded into GeneralParser (below)\\n91:  * if desired.  We don't fold in this manner because all such functions would\\n92:  * be instantiated once per Unit -- but if exactly equivalent code would be\\n93:  * generated (because PerHandlerParser functions have no awareness of Unit),\\n94:  * it's risky to *depend* upon the compiler coalescing the instantiations into\\n95:  * one in the final binary.  PerHandlerParser guarantees no duplication.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * == Parser<ParseHandler, Unit> final → GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> ==\\n98:  *\\n99:  * The final (pun intended) axis of complexity lies in Parser.\\n100:  *\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7cff17db-a98d-4f3a-98b2-06bab02cd492","uuid":"e74d4b90-b4a2-4c0c-b9e5-2228e565b72f","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /* -*- Mode: C++; tab-width: 8; indent-tabs-mode: nil; c-basic-offset: 2 -*-\\n2:  * vim: set ts=8 sts=2 et sw=2 tw=80:\\n3:  * This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public\\n4:  * License, v. 2.0. It stores\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n41:  *\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n44:  * character-type-agnostic. This function calls `CompileGlobalScriptImpl()` which in turn invokes `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate()` (line 302 in BytecodeCompiler.cpp).\\n\\n## Compilation Orchestration: ScriptCompiler\\nThe `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate()` function (line 302) instantiates a `ScriptCompiler<Unit>` class (line 172) and calls its `compile()` method (line 955). The ScriptCompiler extends `SourceAwareCompiler` and orchestrates the entire compilation pipeline.\\n\\n## Parser Entry Points: globalBody and evalBody\\nIn `ScriptCompiler::compile()` (line 955 of BytecodeCompiler.cpp), the parser is invoked:\\n- For global scripts: `parser->globalBody(sc->asGlobalContext())` (line 977)\\n- For eval scripts: `parser->evalBody(sc->asEvalContext())` (line 975)\\n\\nThese methods are defined in `js/src/frontend/Parser.h` in the Parser class (line 1679), which is templatized along the ParseHandler axis (FullParseHandler for full parsing, SyntaxParseHandler for syntax-only parsing) and the Unit axis (character type). The parser converts JavaScript source text into an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) composed of ParseNode objects.\\n\\n## AST Node Types: ParseNode Hierarchy\\nThe AST nodes are defined in `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and include:\\n\\n- **ParseNode** (line 712): Base class for all AST nodes, identified by ParseNodeKind enum. Contains position information (pn_pos), type information (pn_type), and intrinsic links (pn_next).\\n- **UnaryNode** (line 952): Represents unary operations with a single child node (e.g., `!x`, `-y`, `typeof x`)\\n- **BinaryNode** (line 1017): Represents binary operations with left and right child nodes (e.g., `x + y`, `x && y`, `x = y`)\\n- **TernaryNode** (line 1115): Represents ternary conditional operations with three child nodes (e.g., `x ? y : z`)\\n- **ListNode** (line 1184): Represents lists of nodes for statements and expressions (e.g., statement lists, function arguments)\\n- Specialized nodes: **NameNode**, **NumericLiteral**, **StringExpr**, **FunctionNode**, **AssignmentNode**, **ForNode**, **ClassNames**, **ClassMethod**, etc.\\n\\nEach node type implements a `test()` static method for type checking via pattern matching.\\n\\n## Bytecode Emitter: Generating Bytecode\\nAfter successful parsing, `ScriptCompiler::compile()` creates a `BytecodeEmitter` (line 1004) and calls `emitter->emitScript(pn)` (line 1009) to emit bytecode from the AST.\\n\\nThe BytecodeEmitter is defined in `js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h` (line 210) and includes:\\n\\n- Constructor that receives the Parser, SharedContext, and CompilationState (lines 341-350)\\n- The `emitScript()` function (BytecodeEmitter.cpp, line 2354) is the entry point for emitting script bytecode\\n- Helper classes like ClassEmitter, PropertyEmitter, CallOrNewEmitter for specific constructs\\n- Separate prologue and main bytecode sections (lines 96-98 of BytecodeEmitter.h)\\n- Methods to emit individual bytecode instructions corresponding to AST nodes\\n\\n## Bytecode Output: JSScript\\nThe final bytecode is stored in a JSScript object, defined in `js/src/vm/JSScript.h` (line 1787). Key methods:\\n\\n- `JSScript::Create()` (line 1800): Creates a JSScript instance\\n- `JSScript::fullyInitFromStencil()` (line 1818): Initializes JSScript from the compilation stencil\\n- `JSScript::fromStencil()` (line 1826): Allocates and initializes a JSScript with bytecode\\n- `code()` (line 1844): Returns pointer to the bytecode array (`jsbytecode*`), which is an array of uint8_t values representing bytecode instructions\\n- `immutableScriptData()` (line 1839): Returns the immutable script data containing the bytecode\\n\\nThe bytecode can be navigated using `BytecodeLocation` (`js/src/vm/BytecodeLocation.h`) which provides utilities for working with bytecode positions within a JSScript.\\n\\n## Complete Data Flow\\nJavaScript source text → CompileGlobalScript() → CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate() → ScriptCompiler<Unit>::compile() → Parser::globalBody() → ParseNode AST → BytecodeEmitter::emitScript() → Bytecode instructions → JSScript with immutable bytecode array\\n\\nThis modular pipeline allows for lazy compilation of inner functions, separate parsing and bytecode generation phases, and optimization opportunities at each
